CHAPTER 6: CONCLUSION  
The findings of this study successfully align with the primary research objectives, which were 
to explore the impact of dietary components, as measured by the Dietary Inflammatory Index 
(DII), on multimorbidity and to assess the predictive capabilities of machine learning models 
in forecasting multimorbidity based on dietary and demographic factors  using the NHANES 
2015-2018 dataset. The analysis confirms that DII, while not the strongest predictor on its 
own, contributes meaningfully to multimorbidity risk, particularly when interacting with 
demographic variables . Additionally, the machine learning models, particularly Random 
Forest, Neural network , and XGBoost, demonstrated robust performance, validating their 
potential in public health prediction efforts. 
6.1 Research Contributions 
This study makes important contributions to public health and nutrition by establishing a 
strong data-cleaning framework for the NHANES 2015 -2018 dataset, which can enhance 
future research reliability. The DII, alongside factors like BMI, age, gender, and ethnicity, is a 
significant predictor of multimorbidity. It shows that pro-inflammatory diets increase the risk 
of multimorbidity, even after adjusting for demographic factors. ML models like XGBoost, RF, 
and N N showed strong predictive power, with BMI emerging as the dominant predictor. 
Additionally, the study emphasi ses the  superior predictive value of the DII compared to 
broader dietary measures, such as fruit and vegetable consumption. Subgroup analysis 
revealed varied model performance, particularly lower for older populations, underscoring the 
need for tailored public health interventions. These findings are valuable for both healthcare 
providers and policymakers, stressing the need for personali sed nutrition programs and 
targeted prevention strategies to reduce the burden of multimorbidity. 
6.2 Limitations and future research   
This study advances the understanding of dietary inflammation and multimorbidity but has 
some limitations. Self -reported dietary data may introduce inaccuracies, and the cross -
sectional design limits causal inference. Longitudinal studies are needed to est ablish the 
temporal link between diet and multimorbidity. Another restriction is the use of the original 
DII rather than the Energy-Adjusted DII (E-DII) because of data limitations. This is because 
the E-DII needs access to a global energy-adjusted database that was not made available to the 
public. Furthermore, the limited sample size of 6,655 could potentially constrain statistical 
power and generalisability . ML performance also relies on quality of data and model 
generalization, with ethical concerns like privacy and algorithmic biases needing attention. 

--- PAGE 60 ---
Investigating the Impact of Dietary Inflammation on Multimorbidity Using the Dietary Inflammatory Index (DII) and Predicting Multimorbidity with 
Machine Learning: NHANES 2015-2018 
  
Dissertation Task 2 60 2360921 
 
The exclusion of age of onset data due to missing values restricted the ability to explore the 
onset of chronic conditions in detail. 
For future research, incorporating larger and more diverse samples could improve the 
generalizability of findings. Additionally, exploring the use of the E -DII may offer more 
predictive accuracy and provide a clearer understanding of the relationship betwe en diet -
induced inflammation and multimorbidity. Further refinements in machine learning models, 
including the integration of additional features or alternative algorithms, could also enhance 
prediction accuracy.

```{r} 
#Averaging the nutrient intakes for day 1 and day 2 from the 24-hour recall 
NHANES_dataset_final <- NHANES_dataset_rename_nutrients  %>% 
  mutate( 
    alcohol = (alcohol_day_1 + alcohol_day_2) / 2, 
    beta_carotene = (beta_carotene_day_1 + beta_carotene_day_2) / 2, 
    carbohydrate = (carbohydrate_day_1 + carbohydrate_day_2) / 2, 
    cholesterol = (cholesterol_day_1 + cholesterol_day_2) / 2, 
    energy = (energy_day_1 + energy_day_2) / 2, 
    total_fat = (total_fat_day_1 + total_fat_day_2) / 2,

Machine Learning: NHANES 2015-2018 
  
Dissertation Task 2 71 2360921 
 
    dietary_fiber = (dietary_fiber_day_1 + dietary_fiber_day_2) / 2, 
    folic_acid = (folic_acid_day_1 + folic_acid_day_2) / 2, 
    iron = (iron_day_1 + iron_day_2) / 2, 
    magnesium = (magnesium_day_1 + magnesium_day_2) / 2, 
    niacin = (niacin_day_1 + niacin_day_2) / 2, 
    total_mono_unsat_FA = (total_mono_unsat_FA_day_1 + total_mono_unsat_FA_day_2) / 
2, 
    protein = (protein_day_1 + protein_day_2) / 2, 
    selenium = (selenium_day_1 + selenium_day_2) / 2, 
    thiamin_vit_B1 = (thiamin_vit_B1_day_1 + thiamin_vit_B1_day_2) / 2, 
    vit_A_RAE = (vit_A_RAE_day_1 + vit_A_RAE_day_2) / 2, 
    vit_C = (vit_C_day_1 + vit_C_day_2) / 2, 
    vit_D = (vit_D_day_1 + vit_D_day_2) / 2, 
    zinc = (zinc_day_1 + zinc_day_2) / 2, 
    riboflavin_vit_B2 = (riboflavin_vit_B2_day_1 + riboflavin_vit_B2_day_2) / 2, 
    vit_B6 = (vit_B6_day_1 + vit_B6_day_2) / 2, 
    vit_B12 = (vit_B12_day_1 + vit_B12_day_2) / 2, 
    vit_E = (vit_E_day_1 + vit_E_day_2) / 2, 
    total_poly_unsat_FA = (total_poly_unsat_FA_day_1 + total_poly_unsat_FA_day_2) / 2, 
    total_sat_FA = (total_sat_FA_day_1 + total_sat_FA_day_2) / 2, 
    caffeine = (caffeine_day_1 + caffeine_day_2), 
    n3_fat = (n3_fat_day_1 + n3_fat_day_2) / 2, 
    n6_fat = (n6_fat_day_1 + n6_fat_day_2) / 2 
  )
``` 

```{r} 
# Function to calculate pairwise Spearman correlations and p-values for dietary data  
calculate_correlations_and_p_values_dietary_data_NHanes_2015_2016 <- function(data, 
dietary_variables) { 
  cor_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2015_2016 <- matrix(NA, ncol = 
length(dietary_variables), nrow = length(dietary_variables)) 
  p_value_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2015_2016 <- matrix(NA, ncol = 
length(dietary_variables), nrow = length(dietary_variables)) 
  colnames(cor_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2015_2016) <- 
rownames(cor_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2015_2016) <- dietary_variables 
  colnames(p_value_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2015_2016) <- 
rownames(p_value_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2015_2016) <- dietary_variables 
   
  for (i in 1:length(dietary_variables)) { 
    for (j in i:length(dietary_variables)) { 
      if (i == j) { 
        cor_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2015_2016[i, j] <- 1 
        p_value_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2015_2016[i, j] <- NA 
      } else { 
        cor_test <- cor.test(data[[dietary_variables[i]]], data[[dietary_variables[j]]], method = 
"spearman") 
        cor_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2015_2016[i, j] <- 
cor_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2015_2016[j, i] <- cor_test$estimate 
        p_value_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2015_2016[i, j] <- 
p_value_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2015_2016[j, i] <- cor_test$p.value 
      } 
    } 
  } 
  return(list(cor_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2015_2016 = 
cor_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2015_2016, 
p_value_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2015_2016 = 
p_value_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2015_2016)) 
}
``` 

```{r} 
# Calculate standardized scores (z-scores) for each nutrient intake 
NHANES_dataset_final <- NHANES_dataset_final %>% 
  mutate( 
    z_alcohol = (alcohol - global_daily_mean_intake["mean_alcohol"]) / 
global_sd["sd_alcohol"], 
    z_beta_carotene = (beta_carotene - global_daily_mean_intake["mean_beta_carotene"]) / 
global_sd["sd_beta_carotene"], 
    z_carbohydrate = (carbohydrate - global_daily_mean_intake["mean_carbohydrate"]) / 
global_sd["sd_carbohydrate"], 
    z_cholesterol = (cholesterol - global_daily_mean_intake["mean_cholesterol"]) / 
global_sd["sd_cholesterol"], 
    z_energy = (energy - global_daily_mean_intake["mean_energy"]) / 
global_sd["sd_energy"], 
    z_total_fat = (total_fat - global_daily_mean_intake["mean_total_fat"]) / 
global_sd["sd_total_fat"], 
    z_dietary_fiber = (dietary_fiber - global_daily_mean_intake["mean_dietary_fiber"]) / 
global_sd["sd_dietary_fiber"], 
    z_folic_acid = (folic_acid - global_daily_mean_intake["mean_folic_acid"]) / 
global_sd["sd_folic_acid"], 
    z_iron = (iron - global_daily_mean_intake["mean_iron"]) / global_sd["sd_iron"], 
    z_magnesium = (magnesium - global_daily_mean_intake["mean_magnesium"]) / 
global_sd["sd_magnesium"], 
    z_niacin = (niacin - global_daily_mean_intake["mean_niacin"]) / global_sd["sd_niacin"],

global_daily_mean_intake["mean_total_mono_unsat_FA"]) / 
global_sd["sd_total_mono_unsat_FA"],

global_sd["sd_protein"],

global_sd["sd_selenium"],
``` 

```{r} 
# Read the .xpt file 
data <- read_xpt("DIQ_J.xpt") #diabetes

data_3<- read_xpt("KIQ_U_J.xpt") #ckd 
data_4<- read_xpt("WHQ_J.xpt") # weight history 
data_5<- read_xpt("BPX_J.xpt") #hypertension(BP) 
data_6<- read_xpt("DEMO_J.xpt") #demographics(age,sex,ethnicity) 
data_7<- read_xpt("DR1TOT_J.xpt") # dietary_data day1 
data_8<- read_xpt("DR2TOT_J.xpt") # dietary_data day 2 
 
# Ensure all columns are properly converted to standard types 
data <- data %>% mutate(across(everything(), as.character)) 
data_2<-data_2 %>% mutate(across(everything(), as.character)) 
data_3<-data_3 %>% mutate(across(everything(), as.character)) 
data_4<-data_4 %>% mutate(across(everything(), as.character)) 
data_5<-data_5 %>% mutate(across(everything(), as.character)) 
data_6<-data_6 %>% mutate(across(everything(), as.character)) 
data_7<-data_7 %>% mutate(across(everything(), as.character)) 
data_8<-data_8 %>% mutate(across(everything(), as.character)) 
 
# Write the data to a .csv file 
write.csv(data, "diabetes-data_17-18.csv", row.names = FALSE) 
write.csv(data_2, "medical-conditions-data_17-18.csv", row.names = FALSE) 
write.csv(data_3, "chronic-kidney-disease-data_17-18.csv", row.names = FALSE) 
write.csv(data_4, "weight-history-data_17-18.csv", row.names = FALSE)
``` 

```{r} 
#Averaging the nutrient intakes for day 1 and day 2 from the 24-hour recall 
NHANES_dataset_final <- NHANES_dataset_rename_nutrients  %>% 
  mutate( 
    alcohol = (alcohol_day_1 + alcohol_day_2) / 2, 
    beta_carotene = (beta_carotene_day_1 + beta_carotene_day_2) / 2, 
    carbohydrate = (carbohydrate_day_1 + carbohydrate_day_2) / 2, 
    cholesterol = (cholesterol_day_1 + cholesterol_day_2) / 2, 
    energy = (energy_day_1 + energy_day_2) / 2, 
    total_fat = (total_fat_day_1 + total_fat_day_2) / 2, 
    dietary_fiber = (dietary_fiber_day_1 + dietary_fiber_day_2) / 2, 
    folic_acid = (folic_acid_day_1 + folic_acid_day_2) / 2, 
    iron = (iron_day_1 + iron_day_2) / 2, 
    magnesium = (magnesium_day_1 + magnesium_day_2) / 2, 
    niacin = (niacin_day_1 + niacin_day_2) / 2, 
    total_mono_unsat_FA = (total_mono_unsat_FA_day_1 + total_mono_unsat_FA_day_2) / 
2, 
    protein = (protein_day_1 + protein_day_2) / 2, 
    selenium = (selenium_day_1 + selenium_day_2) / 2, 
    thiamin_vit_B1 = (thiamin_vit_B1_day_1 + thiamin_vit_B1_day_2) / 2, 
    vit_A_RAE = (vit_A_RAE_day_1 + vit_A_RAE_day_2) / 2, 
    vit_C = (vit_C_day_1 + vit_C_day_2) / 2, 
    vit_D = (vit_D_day_1 + vit_D_day_2) / 2, 
    zinc = (zinc_day_1 + zinc_day_2) / 2, 
    riboflavin_vit_B2 = (riboflavin_vit_B2_day_1 + riboflavin_vit_B2_day_2) / 2, 
    vit_B6 = (vit_B6_day_1 + vit_B6_day_2) / 2, 
    vit_B12 = (vit_B12_day_1 + vit_B12_day_2) / 2, 

--- PAGE 89 ---
Investigating the Impact of Dietary Inflammation on Multimorbidity Using the Dietary Inflammatory Index (DII) and Predicting Multimorbidity with 
Machine Learning: NHANES 2015-2018 
  
Dissertation Task 2 89 2360921 
 
    vit_E = (vit_E_day_1 + vit_E_day_2) / 2, 
    total_poly_unsat_FA = (total_poly_unsat_FA_day_1 + total_poly_unsat_FA_day_2) / 2, 
    total_sat_FA = (total_sat_FA_day_1 + total_sat_FA_day_2) / 2, 
    caffeine = (caffeine_day_1 + caffeine_day_2), 
    n3_fat = (n3_fat_day_1 + n3_fat_day_2) / 2, 
    n6_fat = (n6_fat_day_1 + n6_fat_day_2) / 2 
  )
``` 

```{r} 
# Function to calculate pairwise Spearman correlations and p-values for dietary data  
calculate_correlations_and_p_values_dietary_data_NHanes_2017_2018 <- function(data, 
dietary_variables) { 
  cor_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2017_2018 <- matrix(NA, ncol = 
length(dietary_variables), nrow = length(dietary_variables)) 
  p_value_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2017_2018 <- matrix(NA, ncol = 
length(dietary_variables), nrow = length(dietary_variables)) 
  colnames(cor_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2017_2018) <- 
rownames(cor_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2017_2018) <- dietary_variables 
  colnames(p_value_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2017_2018) <- 
rownames(p_value_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2017_2018) <- dietary_variables 
   
  for (i in 1:length(dietary_variables)) { 
    for (j in i:length(dietary_variables)) { 
      if (i == j) { 
        cor_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2017_2018[i, j] <- 1 
        p_value_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2017_2018[i, j] <- NA 
      } else { 
        cor_test <- cor.test(data[[dietary_variables[i]]], data[[dietary_variables[j]]], method = 
"spearman") 
        cor_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2017_2018[i, j] <- 
cor_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2017_2018[j, i] <- cor_test$estimate 
        p_value_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2017_2018[i, j] <- 
p_value_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2017_2018[j, i] <- cor_test$p.value 
      } 
    } 
  } 
  return(list(cor_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2017_2018 = 
cor_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2017_2018, 
p_value_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2017_2018 = 
p_value_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2017_2018)) 
} 
 
# Defining dietary variables 
dietary_data_NHanes_2017_2018 <- c( "alcohol", "beta_carotene", "carbohydrate", 
"cholesterol",  
                       "energy", "total_fat", "dietary_fiber", "folic_acid", "iron",  
                       "magnesium", "niacin", "total_mono_unsat_FA", "protein",  
                       "selenium", "thiamin_vit_B1", "vit_A_RAE", "vit_C", "vit_D",  
                       "zinc", "riboflavin_vit_B2", "vit_B6", "vit_B12", "vit_E",  
                       "total_poly_unsat_FA", "total_sat_FA", "caffeine", "n3_fat", "n6_fat") 
 
# Calculating the correlation matrix and p-value matrix  for dietary variables 

--- PAGE 91 ---
Investigating the Impact of Dietary Inflammation on Multimorbidity Using the Dietary Inflammatory Index (DII) and Predicting Multimorbidity with

Dissertation Task 2 91 2360921 
 
results <- 
calculate_correlations_and_p_values_dietary_data_NHanes_2017_2018(NHANES_dataset_f
inal, dietary_data_NHanes_2017_2018) 
correlation_matrix <- results$cor_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2017_2018 
p_value_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2017_2018 <- 
results$p_value_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2017_2018 
 
# Converting the correlation matrix to a long format for ggplot 
melted_correlation_matrix_for_dietary_data_NHanes_2017_2018 <- 
melt(correlation_matrix) 
 
# Plot the correlation matrix heatmap  
ggplot(data = melted_correlation_matrix_for_dietary_data_NHanes_2017_2018, aes(x = 
Var1, y = Var2, fill = value)) + 
  geom_tile(color = "white") + 
  scale_fill_gradient2(low = "blue", high = "red", mid = "white",  
                       midpoint = 0, limit = c(-1, 1), space = "Lab",  
                       name = "Correlation") + 
  theme_minimal() +  
  theme(axis.text.x = element_text(angle = 90, vjust = 1,  
                                   size = 9, hjust = 1)) + 
  coord_fixed() + 
  labs(title = "Spearman Correlation Matrix Heatmap", 
       x = "Variables", 
       y = "Variables") 
 
# Setting high correlation threshold 
high_correlation_threshold_for_dietary_data_NHanes_2017_2018 <- 0.90 
 
# Finding high correlation pairs 
high_cor_pairs_for_dietary_data_NHanes_2017_2018 <- which(abs(correlation_matrix) > 
high_correlation_threshold_for_dietary_data_NHanes_2017_2018 & abs(correlation_matrix) 
< 1, arr.ind = TRUE) 
 
# Extracting high correlation pairs and their p-values 
high_cor_df_for_dietary_data_NHanes_2017_2018 <- data.frame( 
  Var1 = 
rownames(correlation_matrix)[high_cor_pairs_for_dietary_data_NHanes_2017_2018[, 1]], 
  Var2 = 
colnames(correlation_matrix)[high_cor_pairs_for_dietary_data_NHanes_2017_2018[, 2]], 
  Correlation = correlation_matrix[high_cor_pairs_for_dietary_data_NHanes_2017_2018], 
  P_Value = 
p_value_matrix_for_dietary_data_Nhanes_2017_2018[high_cor_pairs_for_dietary_data_NH
anes_2017_2018]) 
 
# Ensuring one-way correlation by removing duplicates and keeping one p-value 
high_cor_df_for_dietary_data_NHanes_2017_2018 <- 
high_cor_df_for_dietary_data_NHanes_2017_2018[!duplicated(t(apply(high_cor_df_for_diet
ary_data_NHanes_2017_2018[, c("Var1", "Var2")], 1, sort))), ]
``` 

```{r} 
# Calculate standardized scores (z-scores) for each nutrient intake

  mutate( 
    z_alcohol = (alcohol - global_daily_mean_intake["mean_alcohol"]) / 
global_sd["sd_alcohol"], 
    z_beta_carotene = (beta_carotene - global_daily_mean_intake["mean_beta_carotene"]) / 
global_sd["sd_beta_carotene"], 
    z_carbohydrate = (carbohydrate - global_daily_mean_intake["mean_carbohydrate"]) / 
global_sd["sd_carbohydrate"], 
    z_cholesterol = (cholesterol - global_daily_mean_intake["mean_cholesterol"]) / 
global_sd["sd_cholesterol"],

global_sd["sd_energy"],

global_sd["sd_total_fat"],

global_sd["sd_folic_acid"],

    p_alcohol = pnorm(z_alcohol)* 2 - 1, 
    p_beta_carotene = pnorm(z_beta_carotene) * 2 - 1,

    p_energy = pnorm(z_energy) * 2 - 1,

    p_vit_C = pnorm(z_vit_C) * 2 - 1, 
    p_vit_D = pnorm(z_vit_D) * 2 - 1, 
    p_zinc = pnorm(z_zinc) * 2 - 1, 
    p_riboflavin_vit_B2 = pnorm(z_riboflavin_vit_B2) * 2 - 1, 
    p_vit_B6 = pnorm(z_vit_B6) * 2 - 1,

    p_vit_E = pnorm(z_vit_E) * 2 - 1, 
    p_total_poly_unsat_FA = pnorm(z_total_poly_unsat_FA) * 2 - 1, 
    p_total_sat_FA= pnorm(z_total_sat_FA) * 2 - 1, 
    p_caffeine = pnorm(z_caffeine)* 2 - 1, 
    p_n3= pnorm(z_n3) * 2 - 1 
  )
``` 

```{r} 
#Converting weight from pounds to kilograms and height from inches to meters 
NHANES_units_change <- NHANES_combined %>% 
  mutate( 
    weight_kg = weight_in_pounds * 0.453592, 
    height_m = height_in_inches * 0.0254 ) 
 
# Calculating BMI and add it as a new column 
NHANES_BMI <- NHANES_units_change %>% 
  mutate(BMI = weight_kg / (height_m^2)) 
```

```{r} 
###Setting values to NA for age for respondants having the age less than 18 
 
# Recording the number of observations before setting ages less than 18 to NA
``` 

```{r} 
# Create a binary column for obesity based on BMI and age criteria 
NHANES_with_obesity <- NHANES_BMI%>% 
  mutate(obesity = if_else(BMI >= 30 & age_years > 20, 1, 0)) 
``` 
 
```{r} 
####Hypertension filtering for systolic_bp hypertension >=130 mmHG and diastolic_bp 
hypertension>= 80 mmHG and converting it into binary values (0-No, 1-Yes) 
#before doing that we need to average systolic blood pressure readings 1,2,3,4 and diastolic 
blood pressure 1,2,3,4 readings. However, we first check if the hypertension variables have 
any missing values. 
 
# Function to calculate the percentage of missing values 
na_percentage_for_Nhanes <- function(x) { 
  sum(is.na(x)) / length(x) * 100 
} 
 
# Calculating the percentage of missing values for systolic blood pressure readings 
systolic_columns <- grep("systolic_bp_", names(NHANES_with_obesity), value = TRUE) 
na_percentage_systolic <- sapply(NHANES_with_obesity[, systolic_columns], 
na_percentage_for_Nhanes) 
 
# Calculating the percentage of missing values for diastolic blood pressure readings 
diastolic_columns <- grep("diastolic_bp_", names(NHANES_with_obesity), value = TRUE) 
na_percentage_diastolic <- sapply(NHANES_with_obesity[, diastolic_columns], 
na_percentage_for_Nhanes) 
 

--- PAGE 105 ---
Investigating the Impact of Dietary Inflammation on Multimorbidity Using the Dietary Inflammatory Index (DII) and Predicting Multimorbidity with 
Machine Learning: NHANES 2015-2018 
  
Dissertation Task 2 105 2360921 
 
# Print the percentage of missing values for systolic blood pressure 
print(paste("Percentage of NA values in systolic blood pressure columns:",  
            paste(systolic_columns, round(na_percentage_systolic, 2), "%", sep = ": ", collapse = 
", "))) 
 
# Print the percentage of missing values for diastolic blood pressure 
print(paste("Percentage of NA values in diastolic blood pressure columns:",  
            paste(diastolic_columns, round(na_percentage_diastolic, 2), "%", sep = ": ", collapse 
= ", "))) 
 
#since systolic_bp_4 has 93.33: % and diastolic_bp_4 has 93.33: % missing observations. 
We will first remove systolic_bp_4 and diastolic_bp_4 before taking the average  
NHANES_with_obesity <- subset(NHANES_with_obesity, select = -systolic_bp_4) 
NHANES_with_obesity <- subset(NHANES_with_obesity, select = -diastolic_bp_4) 
 
# Calculate the average of the systolic blood pressure measurements 
NHANES_with_obesity$systolic_bp_avg <- rowMeans(NHANES_with_obesity[, 
c("systolic_bp_1", "systolic_bp_2", "systolic_bp_3")], na.rm = TRUE) 
 
# Calculate the average of the diastolic blood pressure measurements 
NHANES_with_obesity$diastolic_bp_avg <- rowMeans(NHANES_with_obesity[, 
c("diastolic_bp_1", "diastolic_bp_2", "diastolic_bp_3")], na.rm = TRUE) 
 
#hypertension filtering for systolic_bp hypertension >=130 mmHG or diastolic_bp 
hypertension>= 80 mmHG 
NHANES_with_hypertension <- NHANES_with_obesity %>% 
  mutate(hypertension = if_else(systolic_bp_avg  >= 130 | diastolic_bp_avg >= 80, 1, 0)) 
``` 
 
```{r} 
 #To ensure uniformity in our analysis, the age_years variable was converted from a 
numerical to a categorical variable. This conversion was necessary because in the NHANES 
dataset, individuals aged 80 and above were all encoded as "80," while others were recorded 
with their exact age. By creating age intervals, we can maintain consistency across the 
dataset. The defined age categories and breaks are as follows: 
 
# Defining age categories and breaks  
age_categories <- c( 
  "Young Adult" = "18-34", 
  "Middle Aged" = "35-54", 
  "Senior" = "55-74", 
  "Elderly" = "75+" 
) 
 
# Converting age from numerical to categorical variable using defined intervals 
NHANES_data_2015_2018 <- NHANES_with_hypertension %>% 
  mutate( 
    age_category = cut( 
      age_years, 
      breaks = c(17, 34, 54, 74, Inf),

      labels = names(age_categories), 
      right = TRUE 
    ) 
  )
``` 

```{r} 
# Creating a directory(as there are too many plots) to store the plots if it doesn't exist 
output_dir <- "Histograms - Numerical_Univariate_Analyses" 
if (!dir.exists(output_dir)) { 
  dir.create(output_dir) 
} 
 
# Loop through each numerical variable and create plots 
for (var in numerical_columns) { 
  # Histogram with ggplot2 
  hist_plots_nhanes <- ggplot(NHANES_final_completed, aes_string(x = var)) + 
    geom_histogram(fill = "blue", color = "black", bins = 30, alpha = 0.7) + 
    labs(title = paste("Histogram of", var), x = var, y = "Count") + 
    theme_bw() 
   
  # Save the histograms for nhanes numerical variables 
  ggsave(filename = paste0(output_dir, "/histogram_", var, ".png"), plot = hist_plots_nhanes, 
width = 7, height = 5) 
   
  # Q-Q Plot with ggplot2 
  qq_plot_nhanes <- ggplot(NHANES_final_completed, aes(sample = get(var))) + 
    stat_qq() + 
    stat_qq_line(color = "steelblue", size = 1) + 
    labs(title = paste("Q-Q Plot of", var), x = "Theoretical Quantiles", y = "Sample Quantiles") 
+ 
    theme_bw() 
   
  # Save the Q-Q plot 
  ggsave(filename = paste0(output_dir, "/qq_plot_", var, ".png"), plot = qq_plot_nhanes, 
width = 7, height = 5) 
} 
 
print("All plots have been saved to the directory.")
``` 

# Kolmogorov-Smirnov test 
```{r} 
# Perform Kolmogorov-Smirnov test for each numerical column 
ks_results_nhanes_numerical_columns <- sapply(numerical_columns, function(column) { 
  ks_test_nhanes <- ks.test(NHANES_final_completed[[column]], "pnorm",  
                     mean = mean(NHANES_final_completed[[column]], na.rm = TRUE),  
                     sd = sd(NHANES_final_completed[[column]], na.rm = TRUE)) 
  return(c(Statistic = ks_test_nhanes$statistic, P_Value = ks_test_nhanes$p.value)) 
}) 
 
# Convert results to a data frame  
ks_nhanes_results_df <- as.data.frame(t(ks_results_nhanes_numerical_columns)) 
ks_nhanes_results_df 
```

```{r} 
# Initializing empty lists to store results 
variance_list <- list() 
sd_list <- list() 
 
# Calculate mean, variance, standard deviation, and p-value for each column 
for (col in numerical_columns) { 
  variance_list[[col]] <- var(NHANES_final_completed[[col]], na.rm = TRUE) 
  sd_list[[col]] <- sd(NHANES_final_completed[[col]], na.rm = TRUE) 
} 
 
# Creating the summary statistics dataframe 
stats_numerical_summary <- data.frame( 
  Variable = numerical_columns, 
  Variance = unlist(variance_list), 
  SD = unlist(sd_list) 
) 
 
stats_numerical_summary
``` 

```{r} 
# Function to calculate pairwise Spearman correlations and p-values  
calculate_correlations_and_p_values_NHanes_2015_2018 <- function(data, variables) { 
  cor_matrix_for_Nhanes_2015_2018 <- matrix(NA, ncol = length(variables), nrow = 
length(variables)) 
  p_value_matrix_for_Nhanes_2015_2018 <- matrix(NA, ncol = length(variables), nrow = 
length(variables)) 
  colnames(cor_matrix_for_Nhanes_2015_2018) <- 
rownames(cor_matrix_for_Nhanes_2015_2018) <- variables 
  colnames(p_value_matrix_for_Nhanes_2015_2018) <- 
rownames(p_value_matrix_for_Nhanes_2015_2018) <- variables 
   
  for (i in 1:length(variables)) { 
    for (j in i:length(variables)) { 
      if (i == j) { 
        cor_matrix_for_Nhanes_2015_2018[i, j] <- 1 
        p_value_matrix_for_Nhanes_2015_2018[i, j] <- NA 
      } else { 
        cor_test <- cor.test(data[[variables[i]]], data[[variables[j]]], method = "spearman") 
        cor_matrix_for_Nhanes_2015_2018[i, j] <- cor_matrix_for_Nhanes_2015_2018[j, i] <- 
cor_test$estimate 
        p_value_matrix_for_Nhanes_2015_2018[i, j] <- 
p_value_matrix_for_Nhanes_2015_2018[j, i] <- cor_test$p.value 
      } 
    } 

--- PAGE 112 ---
Investigating the Impact of Dietary Inflammation on Multimorbidity Using the Dietary Inflammatory Index (DII) and Predicting Multimorbidity with 
Machine Learning: NHANES 2015-2018 
  
Dissertation Task 2 112 2360921 
 
  } 
  return(list(cor_matrix_for_Nhanes_2015_2018 = cor_matrix_for_Nhanes_2015_2018, 
p_value_matrix_for_Nhanes_2015_2018 = p_value_matrix_for_Nhanes_2015_2018)) 
} 
 
# Calculating the correlation matrix and p-value matrix  for nhanes 
results <- 
calculate_correlations_and_p_values_NHanes_2015_2018(NHANES_final_completed 
,numerical_columns) 
correlation_matrix <- results$cor_matrix_for_Nhanes_2015_2018 
p_value_matrix_for_Nhanes_2015_2018 <- results$p_value_matrix_for_Nhanes_2015_2018 
 
# Converting the correlation matrix to a long format for ggplot 
melted_correlation_matrix_for_NHanes_2015_2018 <- melt(correlation_matrix) 
 
# Plot the correlation matrix heatmap  
ggplot(data = melted_correlation_matrix_for_NHanes_2015_2018, aes(x = Var1, y = Var2, 
fill = value)) + 
  geom_tile(color = "white") + 
  scale_fill_gradient2(low = "blue", high = "red", mid = "white",  
                       midpoint = 0, limit = c(-1, 1), space = "Lab",  
                       name = "Correlation") + 
  theme_minimal() +  
  theme(axis.text.x = element_text(angle = 90, vjust = 1,  
                                   size = 9, hjust = 1)) + 
  coord_fixed() + 
  labs(title = "Spearman Correlation Matrix Heatmap", 
       x = "Variables", 
       y = "Variables") 
 
# Setting high correlation threshold 
high_correlation_threshold_for_NHanes_2015_2018 <- 0.80 
 
# Finding high correlation pairs 
high_cor_pairs_for_NHanes_2015_2018 <- which(abs(correlation_matrix) > 
high_correlation_threshold_for_NHanes_2015_2018 & abs(correlation_matrix) < 1, arr.ind = 
TRUE) 
 
# Extracting high correlation pairs and their p-values 
high_cor_df_for_NHanes_2015_2018 <- data.frame( 
  Var1 = rownames(correlation_matrix)[high_cor_pairs_for_NHanes_2015_2018[, 1]], 
  Var2 = colnames(correlation_matrix)[high_cor_pairs_for_NHanes_2015_2018[, 2]], 
  Correlation = correlation_matrix[high_cor_pairs_for_NHanes_2015_2018], 
  P_Value = 
p_value_matrix_for_Nhanes_2015_2018[high_cor_pairs_for_NHanes_2015_2018]) 
 
# Ensuring one-way correlation by removing duplicates and keeping one p-value 
high_cor_df_for_NHanes_2015_2018 <- 
high_cor_df_for_NHanes_2015_2018[!duplicated(t(apply(high_cor_df_for_NHanes_2015_2
018[, c("Var1", "Var2")], 1, sort))), ]
``` 

```{r} 
 
# Define categorical columns for mosaic plot 
NHANES_mosaic_categorical_columns <- c("gender", "ethnicity", "age_category", 
"multimorbidity") 
 
# Generate pairs of categorical columns 
pairs <- combn(NHANES_mosaic_categorical_columns, 2, simplify = TRUE) 
 
# Loop through each pair of categorical variables and create mosaic plots 
for (i in 1:ncol(pairs)) { 
  var1 <- pairs[1, i] 
  var2 <- pairs[2, i] 
   
  # Create a contingency table and convert it to a data frame 
  contingency_table <- table(NHANES_final_completed[[var1]], 
NHANES_final_completed[[var2]]) 
  df_mosaic <- as.data.frame(contingency_table) 
   
  # Rename the columns for consistency with geom_mosaic's requirements 
  colnames(df_mosaic) <- c(var1, var2, "Freq") 
   
  # Check if there is data to plot 
  if (nrow(df_mosaic) > 0) { 
    # Create mosaic plot using ggplot2 and ggmosaic 
    nhanes_mosaic_plot <- ggplot(df_mosaic) + 
      geom_mosaic(aes(weight = Freq, x = product(!!sym(var1)), fill = !!sym(var2)), na.rm = 
TRUE) + 
      scale_fill_brewer(palette = "Set3") + 
      theme_minimal() + 
      theme(axis.text.x = element_text(angle = 45, hjust = 1)) + 
      labs(title = paste("Mosaic Plot of", var1, "vs", var2), 
           x = var1, y = var2, fill = var2)} 
  print(nhanes_mosaic_plot) 
} 
 
```

# DII exploration 
 
#Calculate Quartiles for DII and Categorize Data 
```{r} 
# Calculating quartiles for DII 
DII_quartiles <- quantile(NHANES_final_completed$DII, probs = c(0.25, 0.5, 0.75)) 
DII_quartiles 
 
# Extracting DII_quartiles 
q1 <- DII_quartiles[1]  # 25th percentile (first quartile) 
q2 <- DII_quartiles[2]  # 50th percentile (median, second quartile) 
q3 <- DII_quartiles[3]  # 75th percentile (third quartile) 
 
# Categorizing DII into quartiles based on the calculated quantiles 
NHANES_final_completed <- NHANES_final_completed %>% 
  mutate(DII_quartile = case_when( 
    DII <= q1 ~ "Q1", 
    DII > q1 & DII <= q2 ~ "Q2", 
    DII > q2 & DII <= q3 ~ "Q3", 
    DII > q3 ~ "Q4" 
  )) 
 
# Ensuring the new quartile variable is a factor with ordered levels 
NHANES_final_completed$DII_quartile <- factor(NHANES_final_completed$DII_quartile, 
levels = c("Q1", "Q2", "Q3", "Q4")) 
 
# Print the counts of each quartile 
table(NHANES_final_completed$DII_quartile) 
```

#Calculate Proportions(categorical variables), Means(numerical variable) and statistical 
significance for age, gender, ethnicity,chronic cinditions, BMI by DII Quartiles 
 
```{r} 
# Function to calculate proportions for  categorical variable and perform Chi-Square test 
calculate_proportions_and_pvalue_for_nhanes <- function(data, variable) { 
   
  prop_table <- prop.table(table(data$DII_quartile, data[[variable]])) * 100   # Calculating 
proportions 
  prop <- round(prop_table, 2) 
  chi_square_test <- chisq.test(table(data$DII_quartile, data[[variable]])) # Performing Chi-
Square test 
  p_value_chi_square <- round(chi_square_test$p.value, 4) 
  return(list(prop = prop, p_value_chi_square = p_value_chi_square)) 
} 
 
# Define levels for age, gender, and ethnicity 
age_levels <- c("Young Adult", "Middle Aged", "Senior", "Elderly") 
gender_levels <- c("Male", "Female") 
ethnicity_levels <- c("Mexican American", "Non-Hispanic Asian", "Non-Hispanic Black", 
"Non-Hispanic White", "Other Hispanic", "Other Race (IMR)") 
chronic_conditions <- c("diabetes", "asthma", "arthritis", "COPD", "cancer", "stroke", 
"coronary_heart_disease", "liver_condition", "failing_kidneys", "hypertension", "obesity") 
 
# Get results for each category 
age_results <- calculate_proportions_and_pvalue_for_nhanes(NHANES_final_completed, 
"age_category") 
gender_results <-calculate_proportions_and_pvalue_for_nhanes(NHANES_final_completed, 
"gender") 
ethnicity_results <- 
calculate_proportions_and_pvalue_for_nhanes(NHANES_final_completed, "ethnicity") 
chronic_conditions_results <- lapply(chronic_conditions, function(cond) 
calculate_proportions_and_pvalue_for_nhanes(NHANES_final_completed, cond)) 
 
# Output each result 
print("Age Category Proportions and P-Value:") 
print(age_results$prop) 
print(paste("P-Value:", age_results$p_value_chi_square)) 
 
print("Gender Proportions and P-Value:") 
print(gender_results$prop) 
print(paste("P-Value:", gender_results$p_value_chi_square)) 
 
print("Ethnicity Proportions and P-Value:") 
print(ethnicity_results$prop) 
print(paste("P-Value:", ethnicity_results$p_value_chi_square))

Investigating the Impact of Dietary Inflammation on Multimorbidity Using the Dietary Inflammatory Index (DII) and Predicting Multimorbidity with

print("Chronic Conditions Proportions and P-Values:") 
for (i in 1:length(chronic_conditions)) { 
  print(paste(chronic_conditions[i], "Proportions:")) 
  print(chronic_conditions_results[[i]]$prop) 
  print(paste("P-Value:", chronic_conditions_results[[i]]$p_value_chi_square))

#### Calculate means and standard deviations for BMI by DII quartile 
means <- aggregate(NHANES_final_completed$BMI, by = 
list(NHANES_final_completed$DII_quartile), FUN = mean, na.rm = TRUE) 
sds <- aggregate(NHANES_final_completed$BMI, by = 
list(NHANES_final_completed$DII_quartile), FUN = sd, na.rm = TRUE) 
mean_sd_BMI <- paste0(round(means$x, 2), " ± ", round(sds$x, 2)) 
 
# Perform ANOVA to compare means across DII quartiles 
aov_test <- aov(BMI ~ DII_quartile, data = NHANES_final_completed) 
p_value_ANOVA <- round(summary(aov_test)[[1]][["Pr(>F)"]][1], 4) 
 
mean_sd_BMI  
p_value_ANOVA  
``` 
 
#EDA FOR MULTIMORBIDITY 
 
# Mann-Whitney U Test 
*P_value_MW: A small p-value (typically < 0.05) suggests that there is a statistically 
significant difference between the distributions of the numerical variable for the two groups 
(i.e., "yes" or "no" for multimorbidity).* 
```{r} 
# Initializing empty lists to store results 
p_values_nhanes_mw_list<- list() 
 
# Calculating Mann-Whitney U test p-value for each column 
for (col in numerical_columns) { 
  p_values_nhanes_mw_list[[col]] <- wilcox.test(NHANES_final_completed[[col]] ~ 
NHANES_final_completed$multimorbidity)$p.value # Mann-Whitney U test 
} 
 
# Creating dataframe with Mann-Whitney p-values 
nhanes_stats_summary_mw <- data.frame( 
  Variable = numerical_columns, 
  P_value_MW = unlist(p_values_nhanes_mw_list)) 
 
nhanes_stats_summary_mw 
``` 
 
#Chi-Square Test for Categorical Variables and multimorbidity 
 
```{r} 
# Defining your disease variables and the multimorbidity variable 

--- PAGE 119 ---
Investigating the Impact of Dietary Inflammation on Multimorbidity Using the Dietary Inflammatory Index (DII) and Predicting Multimorbidity with 
Machine Learning: NHANES 2015-2018 
  
Dissertation Task 2 119 2360921 
 
categorical_variables_excluding_multimorbidity <- c("diabetes", "asthma", "arthritis", 
"COPD", "cancer", "stroke", "coronary_heart_disease", "liver_condition", 
"failing_kidneys","hypertension", "obesity","gender", "ethnicity", "age_category") 
 
# Initializing a list to store results 
chi_square_results <- list() 
 
# Creating a contingency table 
for (category in categorical_variables_excluding_multimorbidity) { 
  contingency_table <- table(NHANES_final_completed[[category]], 
NHANES_final_completed$multimorbidity) 
   
  chi_test <- chisq.test(contingency_table)  # Performing the chi-square test 
   
  chi_square_results[[category]] <- list( 
    p_value = chi_test$p.value, 
    chi_square_statistic = chi_test$statistic, 
    degrees_of_freedom = chi_test$parameter, 
    contingency_table = contingency_table 
  ) 
} 
 
for (category in categorical_variables_excluding_multimorbidity) { 
  cat(category) 
  cat("\nChi-Square Statistic:", chi_square_results[[category]]$chi_square_statistic) 
  cat("\nDegrees of Freedom:", chi_square_results[[category]]$degrees_of_freedom) 
  cat("\nP-Value:", chi_square_results[[category]]$p_value) 
  cat("\nContingency Table:\n") 
  print(chi_square_results[[category]]$contingency_table) 
} 
``` 
 
# Bar Plot for Chi-Square Statistics

```{r} 
# Extracting chi-square statistics and category names

# Creating a data frame for plotting 
chi_square_nhanes_df <- data.frame( 
  Category = category_names_nhanes,
``` 

#Preliminary Model Fitting 
#logistic regression model 
```{r} 
# Initializing lists to store results 
model_names <- c("Only DII", "With Covariates", "With Interactions") 
mcfadden_r2_list <- c() 
model_summaries <- list() 
 
# Defining the models 
model_formulas <- list( 
  "Only DII" = multimorbidity ~ DII, 
  "With Covariates" = multimorbidity ~ DII + age_category + BMI + gender + ethnicity, 
  "With Interactions" = multimorbidity ~ DII * age_category + DII * BMI + DII * gender + 
DII * ethnicity 
) 
 
# Fitting, calculating metrics, and storing results for each model 
for (i in 1:length(model_names)) { 
  # Fit the model using standard glm for logistic regression 
  model <- glm(model_formulas[[i]], data = NHANES_final_completed, family = binomial) 
  model_summaries[[i]] <- summary(model) 
   

--- PAGE 121 ---
Investigating the Impact of Dietary Inflammation on Multimorbidity Using the Dietary Inflammatory Index (DII) and Predicting Multimorbidity with 
Machine Learning: NHANES 2015-2018 
  
Dissertation Task 2 121 2360921 
 
  # Calculating McFadden's R-squared 
  logLik_model <- logLik(model) 
  logLik_null <- logLik(glm(multimorbidity ~ 1, data = NHANES_final_completed, family = 
binomial)) 
  mcfadden_r2 <- 1 - (as.numeric(logLik_model) / as.numeric(logLik_null)) 
  mcfadden_r2_list <- c(mcfadden_r2_list, mcfadden_r2) 
} 
 
# Displaying model summaries and McFadden's R-squared 
for (i in 1:length(model_summaries)) { 
  print(paste("Summary for", model_names[i])) 
  print(model_summaries[[i]]) 
  print(paste("McFadden's R-squared for", model_names[i], ":", round(mcfadden_r2_list[i], 
4))) 
} 
```

#NEURAL NETWORK TO PREDICT MULTIMORBIDITY

```{r} 
set.seed(124)

train_data$gender <- as.factor(train_data$gender)

nn_test_data_transformed_feature_set_1  <- data.frame(predict(dmy, newdata = test_data))
``` 

```{r}

  booster = "gbtree",       # Using trees

  max_depth = 6,            # Maximum depth of a tree 
  gamma = 1,                # Minimum loss reduction required to make a further partition 
  subsample = 0.8,          # Subsample ratio of the training instance 
  colsample_bytree = 0.8,   # Subsample ratio of columns when constructing each tree 
  eval_metric = "error"     # Evaluation metric 
) 
 
#Training the XGBoost Model 
 
 
xgb_feature_set_1_bst_model <- xgb.train( 
  params = xgb_feature_set_1_params, 
  data = xgb_feature_set_1_dtrain, 
  nrounds = 100, # Number of boosting rounds 
  watchlist = list(train = xgb_feature_set_1_dtrain, eval = xgb_feature_set_1_dtest), 
  early_stopping_rounds = 10,  
  print_every_n = 10

)
``` 

```{r} 
# Setting a seed before cross-validation for consistency 
set.seed(124) 
# Perform Cross-Validation 
cv_xgb_feature_set_1_results <- xgb.cv( 
  params = xgb_feature_set_1_params, 
  data = xgb_feature_set_1_dtrain, 
  nrounds = 100,   
  nfold = 5,  # 5-fold cross-validation 
  showsd = TRUE,   
  stratified = TRUE,  # Perform stratified sampling 
  early_stopping_rounds = 10,  # Stop early if no improvement 
  maximize = FALSE,  # Minimize the error metric 
  print_every_n = 10  # Print progress every 10 rounds 
) 
 
# Best number of rounds based on CV 
cv_xgb_feature_set_1_best_nrounds <- cv_xgb_feature_set_1_results$best_iteration 
print(paste("Best number of rounds:", cv_xgb_feature_set_1_best_nrounds)) 
 
# Training the final model using the best number of rounds 
cv_xgb_feature_set_1_bst_model <- xgb.train( 
  params = xgb_feature_set_1_params, 
  data = xgb_feature_set_1_dtrain, 
  nrounds = cv_xgb_feature_set_1_best_nrounds, 
  watchlist = list(train = xgb_feature_set_1_dtrain, eval = xgb_feature_set_1_dtest), 
  early_stopping_rounds = 10, 
  print_every_n = 10) 
 
# Predictions 
cv_xgb_feature_set_1_preds <- predict(cv_xgb_feature_set_1_bst_model, 
xgb_feature_set_1_dtest) 
cv_xgb_feature_set_1_preds_binary <- ifelse(cv_xgb_feature_set_1_preds > 0.5, 1, 0) 
 
# Evaluate the Model
``` 

#XGBoost MODEL 
```{r} 
set.seed(124) 
# Convert categorical variables to factors  
train_data$age_category <- as.factor(train_data$age_category) 
train_data$gender <- as.factor(train_data$gender) 
train_data$ethnicity <- as.factor(train_data$ethnicity) 
train_data$DII_quartile <- as.factor(train_data$DII_quartile) 
train_data$multimorbidity <- as.factor(train_data$multimorbidity) 
 
test_data$age_category <- as.factor(test_data$age_category) 
test_data$gender <- as.factor(test_data$gender) 
test_data$ethnicity <- as.factor(test_data$ethnicity) 
test_data$DII_quartile <- as.factor(test_data$DII_quartile) 
test_data$multimorbidity <- as.factor(test_data$multimorbidity) 
 
# One-hot encode categorical variables 
dmy <- dummyVars(" ~ .", data = train_data) 
xgb_train_data_transformed_feature_set_2 <- data.frame(predict(dmy, newdata = 
train_data)) 
xgb_test_data_transformed_feature_set_2 <- data.frame(predict(dmy, newdata = test_data)) 
 
# Correct the selected features to match the actual column names in the transformed data 
xgb_selected_features_feature_set_2 <- c( 
  "DII_quartile.Q1", 
  "DII_quartile.Q2", 

--- PAGE 139 ---
Investigating the Impact of Dietary Inflammation on Multimorbidity Using the Dietary Inflammatory Index (DII) and Predicting Multimorbidity with 
Machine Learning: NHANES 2015-2018 
  
Dissertation Task 2 139 2360921 
 
  "DII_quartile.Q3", 
  "DII_quartile.Q4", 
  "BMI", 
  "age_category.Middle.Aged",  
  "age_category.Senior",  
  "age_category.Young.Adult",  
  "age_category.Elderly", 
  "gender.male",  
  "gender.female",  
  "ethnicity.Non.Hispanic.Asian",  
  "ethnicity.Non.Hispanic.Black",  
  "ethnicity.Non.Hispanic.White",  
  "ethnicity.Mexican.American", 
  "ethnicity.Other.Hispanic",  
  "ethnicity.Other.Race.IMR." 
) 
 
# Ensuring only the selected features are used 
xgb_train_matrix_feature_set_2  <- 
as.matrix(xgb_train_data_transformed_feature_set_2[xgb_selected_features_feature_set_2]) 
xgb_train_label_feature_set_2 <- ifelse(train_data$multimorbidity == "yes", 1, 0) 
 
xgb_test_matrix_feature_set_2 <- 
as.matrix(xgb_test_data_transformed_feature_set_2[xgb_selected_features_feature_set_2]) 
xgb_test_label_feature_set_2 <- ifelse(test_data$multimorbidity == "yes", 1, 0) 
 
#Creating DMatrix for XGBoost 
xgb_feature_set_2_dtrain <- xgb.DMatrix(data = xgb_train_matrix_feature_set_2, label = 
xgb_train_label_feature_set_2) 
xgb_feature_set_2_dtest <- xgb.DMatrix(data = xgb_test_matrix_feature_set_2 , label = 
xgb_test_label_feature_set_2) 
 
#Setting Parameters for XGBoost 
xgb_feature_set_2_params <- list( 
  booster = "gbtree",       
  objective = "binary:logistic",   
  eta = 0.1,              
  max_depth = 6,             
  gamma = 1,                 
  subsample = 0.8,           
  colsample_bytree = 0.8,    
  eval_metric = "error"      
) 
 
#Training the XGBoost Model 
xgb_feature_set_2_bst_model <- xgb.train( 
  params = xgb_feature_set_2_params, 
  data = xgb_feature_set_2_dtrain, 
  nrounds = 100, # Number of boosting rounds 
  watchlist = list(train = xgb_feature_set_2_dtrain, eval = xgb_feature_set_2_dtest), 

--- PAGE 140 ---
Investigating the Impact of Dietary Inflammation on Multimorbidity Using the Dietary Inflammatory Index (DII) and Predicting Multimorbidity with 
Machine Learning: NHANES 2015-2018 
  
Dissertation Task 2 140 2360921 
 
  early_stopping_rounds = 10,  
  print_every_n = 10 
) 
 
# Predicting the probabilities on the test set 
xgb_feature_set_2_preds <- predict(xgb_feature_set_2_bst_model, xgb_feature_set_2_dtest) 
 
# Convert probabilities to binary labels 
xgb_feature_set_2_preds_binary <- ifelse(xgb_feature_set_2_preds > 0.5, 1, 0) 
 
## Evaluate model performance 
conf_matrix_xgb_feature_set_2<- confusionMatrix(factor(xgb_feature_set_2_preds_binary), 
factor(xgb_test_label_feature_set_2, levels = c(0, 1)),positive = "1") 
conf_matrix_xgb_feature_set_2 
``` 
 
 
```{r} 
# Setting a seed before cross-validation for consistency 
set.seed(124) 
# Perform Cross-Validation 
cv_xgb_feature_set_2_results <- xgb.cv( 
  params = xgb_feature_set_2_params, 
  data = xgb_feature_set_2_dtrain, 
  nrounds = 100,   
  nfold = 5,  
  showsd = TRUE,   
  stratified = TRUE,  
  early_stopping_rounds = 10,   
  maximize = FALSE,   
  print_every_n = 10   
) 
 
# Best number of rounds based on CV 
cv_xgb_feature_set_2_best_nrounds <- cv_xgb_feature_set_2_results$best_iteration 
print(paste("Best number of rounds:", cv_xgb_feature_set_2_best_nrounds)) 
 
# Training the final model using the best number of rounds 
cv_xgb_feature_set_2_bst_model <- xgb.train( 
  params = xgb_feature_set_2_params, 
  data = xgb_feature_set_2_dtrain, 
  nrounds = cv_xgb_feature_set_2_best_nrounds, 
  watchlist = list(train = xgb_feature_set_2_dtrain, eval = xgb_feature_set_2_dtest), 
  early_stopping_rounds = 10, 
  print_every_n = 10) 
 
# Predictions 
cv_xgb_feature_set_2_preds <- predict(cv_xgb_feature_set_2_bst_model, 
xgb_feature_set_2_dtest) 
cv_xgb_feature_set_2_preds_binary <- ifelse(cv_xgb_feature_set_2_preds > 0.5, 1, 0)
``` 

#DECISION TREE TO PREDICT MULTIMORBIDITY  
```{r} 
# Define the formula for the model 
feature_set_3 <- multimorbidity ~ DII_quartile + age_category + BMI_category + gender + 
ethnicity  
 
# Train the decision tree model 
decision_tree_model_feature_set_3_train <- rpart(feature_set_3, 
                                   data = train_data,  
                                   method = "class",  
                                   control = rpart.control(cp = 0.01)) 
# Visualize the decision tree 
rpart.plot(decision_tree_model_feature_set_3_train,  
           main = "Decision Tree for Multimorbidity", 
           type = 3,  
           extra = 104, 
           under = TRUE,  
           faclen = 0) 
 
# Predict on the test data 
decision_tree_feature_set_3_pred <- predict(decision_tree_model_feature_set_3_train, 
test_data[,-which(names(test_data) == "multimorbidity")], type= "class") 
 
# Evaluate model performance
``` 

#NEURAL NETWORK TO PREDICT MULTIMORBIDITY 
```{r} 
set.seed(124) 
 
# Convert categorical variables to factors 
train_data$age_category <- as.factor(train_data$age_category) 
train_data$gender <- as.factor(train_data$gender) 
train_data$ethnicity <- as.factor(train_data$ethnicity) 
train_data$multimorbidity <- as.factor(train_data$multimorbidity) 
train_data$BMI_category <- as.factor(train_data$BMI_category) 
train_data$DII_quartile <- as.factor(train_data$DII_quartile) 

--- PAGE 146 ---
Investigating the Impact of Dietary Inflammation on Multimorbidity Using the Dietary Inflammatory Index (DII) and Predicting Multimorbidity with

test_data$DII_quartile <- as.factor(test_data$DII_quartile) 
test_data$BMI_category <- as.factor(test_data$BMI_category)

# One-hot encode categorical variables 
dmy <- dummyVars(" ~ .", data = train_data) 
nn_train_data_transformed_feature_set_3<- data.frame(predict(dmy, newdata = train_data)) 
nn_test_data_transformed_feature_set_3  <- data.frame(predict(dmy, newdata = test_data)) 
 
# Correct the selected features to match the actual column names in the transformed data 
nn_selected_features_feature_set_3 <- c( 
  "DII_quartile.Q1", 
  "DII_quartile.Q2", 
  "DII_quartile.Q3", 
  "DII_quartile.Q4", 
  "BMI_category.Underweight", 
  "BMI_category.Normal.weight",  
  "BMI_category.Overweight", 
  "age_category.Middle.Aged",  
  "age_category.Senior",  
  "age_category.Young.Adult",  
  "age_category.Elderly", 
  "gender.male",  
  "gender.female",  
  "ethnicity.Non.Hispanic.Asian",  
  "ethnicity.Non.Hispanic.Black",  
  "ethnicity.Non.Hispanic.White",  
  "ethnicity.Mexican.American", 
  "ethnicity.Other.Hispanic",  
  "ethnicity.Other.Race.IMR." 
) 
 
#  extracting the feature matrix 
nn_train_matrix_feature_set_3 <- 
as.matrix(nn_train_data_transformed_feature_set_3[nn_selected_features_feature_set_3 ]) 
nn_test_matrix_feature_set_3  <- as.matrix(nn_test_data_transformed_feature_set_3 
[nn_selected_features_feature_set_3 ]) 
 
# Normalizing the data 
preProc <- preProcess(nn_train_matrix_feature_set_3, method = c("center", "scale")) 
nn_train_matrix_feature_set_3 <- predict(preProc, nn_train_matrix_feature_set_3) 
nn_test_matrix_feature_set_3  <- predict(preProc, nn_test_matrix_feature_set_3 ) 
 
# Extracting the target variable 
nn_train_label_feature_set_3 <- class.ind(train_data$multimorbidity) 
nn_test_label_feature_set_3 <- test_data$multimorbidity 

--- PAGE 147 ---
Investigating the Impact of Dietary Inflammation on Multimorbidity Using the Dietary Inflammatory Index (DII) and Predicting Multimorbidity with 
Machine Learning: NHANES 2015-2018 
  
Dissertation Task 2 147 2360921 
 
 
# Train the neural network model using nnet 
nn_model_feature_set_3_train <- nnet(nn_train_matrix_feature_set_3, 
nn_train_label_feature_set_3 , size = 5, linout = FALSE, maxit = 200, softmax = TRUE) 
nn_model_feature_set_3_train 
 
# Make predictions on the test set 
nn_feature_set_3_predictions_prob <- predict(nn_model_feature_set_3_train, newdata = 
nn_test_matrix_feature_set_3 , type = "raw") 
nn_feature_set_3_predictions <- apply(nn_feature_set_3_predictions_prob, 1, which.max) 
 
# Convert predictions to factor with correct levels 
nn_feature_set_3_predictions <- factor(nn_feature_set_3_predictions, levels = 
1:nlevels(test_data$multimorbidity), labels = levels(test_data$multimorbidity)) 
 
# Evaluate model performance 
conf_matrix_nn_feature_set_3 <- confusionMatrix(factor(nn_feature_set_3_predictions), 
factor(nn_test_label_feature_set_3), positive = "yes") 
conf_matrix_nn_feature_set_3 
 
# Plot the neural network model 
plotnet(nn_model_feature_set_3_train)
``` 

```{r} 
set.seed(124) 
# cross-validation settings 
train_control_nn_feature_set_3 <- trainControl(method = "cv", number = 5, verboseIter = 
TRUE) 
 
# Cross-validation and training using caret 
cv_nn_model_feature_set_3 <- train(x = nn_train_matrix_feature_set_3,  
                  y = train_data$multimorbidity,  
                  method = "nnet",  
                  trControl = train_control_nn_feature_set_3, 
                  tuneLength = 5,  
                  linout = FALSE, 
                  maxit = 200, 
                  trace = FALSE, 
                  MaxNWts = 10000) 
cv_nn_model_feature_set_3 
 
# predictions on the test set using the cv nn model 
cv_nn_feature_set_3_predictions_prob <- predict(cv_nn_model_feature_set_3 , newdata = 
nn_test_matrix_feature_set_3 , type = "raw") 
cv_nn_feature_set_3_predictions_prob 
 
# Check if predictions are numeric or factors 
if (is.numeric(cv_nn_feature_set_3_predictions_prob)) { 
  # If predictions are probabilities, convert them to class labels based on a threshold 

--- PAGE 148 ---
Investigating the Impact of Dietary Inflammation on Multimorbidity Using the Dietary Inflammatory Index (DII) and Predicting Multimorbidity with 
Machine Learning: NHANES 2015-2018 
  
Dissertation Task 2 148 2360921 
 
  cv_nn_feature_set_3_predictions <- ifelse(cv_nn_feature_set_3_predictions_prob > 0.5, 
"yes", "no") 
} else { 
  # If predictions are already class labels (factors), use them directly 
  cv_nn_feature_set_3_predictions <- cv_nn_feature_set_3_predictions_prob 
} 
 
# Ensuring predictions are factors with the correct levels 
cv_nn_predictions_feature_set_3 <- factor(cv_nn_feature_set_3_predictions, levels = c("no", 
"yes")) 
 
# Ensuring test_label is a factor with the correct levels 
cv_nn_test_label_feature_set_3 <- factor(test_data$multimorbidity, levels = c("no", "yes")) 
 
# Evaluate model performance
``` 

```{r} 
  early_stopping_rounds = 10,

)
``` 

#NEURAL NETWORK TO PREDICT MULTIMORBIDITY 
```{r} 
set.seed(124)

train_data$age_category <- as.factor(train_data$age_category)

test_data$ethnicity <- as.factor(test_data$ethnicity) 
test_data$multimorbidity <- as.factor(test_data$multimorbidity)

nn_train_data_transformed_feature_set_4<- data.frame(predict(dmy, newdata = train_data)) 
nn_test_data_transformed_feature_set_4 <- data.frame(predict(dmy, newdata = test_data)) 
 
# Correct the selected features to match the actual column names in the transformed data

  "DII",  
  "BMI", 
  "age_category.Middle.Aged",  
  "age_category.Senior",  
  "age_category.Young.Adult",  
  "age_category.Elderly", 
  "gender.male",  
  "gender.female",  
  "ethnicity.Non.Hispanic.Asian",  

--- PAGE 157 ---
Investigating the Impact of Dietary Inflammation on Multimorbidity Using the Dietary Inflammatory Index (DII) and Predicting Multimorbidity with 
Machine Learning: NHANES 2015-2018 
  
Dissertation Task 2 157 2360921 
 
  "ethnicity.Non.Hispanic.Black",  
  "ethnicity.Non.Hispanic.White",  
  "ethnicity.Mexican.American", 
  "ethnicity.Other.Hispanic",  
  "ethnicity.Other.Race.IMR." 
) 
 
#  extracting the feature matrix 
nn_train_matrix_feature_set_4 <- 
as.matrix(nn_train_data_transformed_feature_set_4[nn_selected_features_feature_set_4 ]) 
nn_test_matrix_feature_set_4 <- as.matrix(nn_test_data_transformed_feature_set_4 
[nn_selected_features_feature_set_4 ]) 
 
# Normalizing the data 
preProc <- preProcess(nn_train_matrix_feature_set_4, method = c("center", "scale")) 
nn_train_matrix_feature_set_4 <- predict(preProc, nn_train_matrix_feature_set_4) 
nn_test_matrix_feature_set_4  <- predict(preProc, nn_test_matrix_feature_set_4 )

nn_train_label_feature_set_4 <- class.ind(train_data$multimorbidity)

nn_train_label_feature_set_4 , size = 5, linout = FALSE, maxit = 200, softmax = TRUE) 
nn_model_feature_set_4_train 
 
# Make predictions on the test set

nn_test_matrix_feature_set_4 , type = "raw")

# Convert predictions to factor with correct levels 
nn_feature_set_4_predictions <- factor(nn_feature_set_4_predictions, levels = 
1:nlevels(test_data$multimorbidity), labels = levels(test_data$multimorbidity)) 
 
# Evaluate model performance 
conf_matrix_nn_feature_set_4 <- confusionMatrix(factor(nn_feature_set_4_predictions), 
factor(nn_test_label_feature_set_4), positive = "yes") 
conf_matrix_nn_feature_set_4 
 
# Plot the neural network model 
plotnet(nn_model_feature_set_4_train)
``` 

```{r} 
# Check if predictions are numeric or factors 
if (is.numeric(cv_nn_feature_set_4_predictions_prob)) { 
  # If predictions are probabilities, convert them to class labels based on a threshold 
  cv_nn_feature_set_4_predictions <- ifelse(cv_nn_feature_set_4_predictions_prob > 0.5, 
"yes", "no") 
} else { 
  # If predictions are already class labels (factors), use them directly 
  cv_nn_feature_set_4_predictions <- cv_nn_feature_set_4_predictions_prob 
} 
 
# Ensuring predictions are factors with the correct levels 
cv_nn_predictions_feature_set_4 <- factor(cv_nn_feature_set_4_predictions, levels = c("no", 
"yes")) 
 
# Ensuring test_label is a factor with the correct levels 
cv_nn_test_label_feature_set_4 <- factor(test_data$multimorbidity, levels = c("no", "yes")) 
 
# Evaluate model performance 
conf_matrix_cv_nn_feature_set_4 <- confusionMatrix(cv_nn_predictions_feature_set_4, 
cv_nn_test_label_feature_set_4, positive = "yes") 
conf_matrix_cv_nn_feature_set_4 
```

#XGBoost MODEL 
```{r} 
set.seed(124) 
# Convert categorical variables to factors  
train_data$age_category <- as.factor(train_data$age_category) 
train_data$gender <- as.factor(train_data$gender) 
train_data$ethnicity <- as.factor(train_data$ethnicity) 
train_data$multimorbidity <- as.factor(train_data$multimorbidity) 
 
test_data$age_category <- as.factor(test_data$age_category) 
test_data$gender <- as.factor(test_data$gender) 
test_data$ethnicity <- as.factor(test_data$ethnicity) 
test_data$multimorbidity <- as.factor(test_data$multimorbidity) 
 
# One-hot encode categorical variables 
dmy <- dummyVars(" ~ .", data = train_data) 
xgb_train_data_transformed_feature_set_4 <- data.frame(predict(dmy, newdata = 
train_data)) 
xgb_test_data_transformed_feature_set_4 <- data.frame(predict(dmy, newdata = test_data)) 
 
# Correct the selected features to match the actual column names in the transformed data 
xgb_selected_features_feature_set_4 <- c( 
  "DII", 
  "BMI", 
  "age_category.Middle.Aged",  
  "age_category.Senior",  
  "age_category.Young.Adult",  
  "age_category.Elderly", 
  "gender.male",  
  "gender.female",  
  "ethnicity.Non.Hispanic.Asian",  
  "ethnicity.Non.Hispanic.Black",  
  "ethnicity.Non.Hispanic.White",  
  "ethnicity.Mexican.American", 
  "ethnicity.Other.Hispanic",  
  "ethnicity.Other.Race.IMR." 
) 
 
# Ensuring only the selected features are used 
xgb_train_matrix_feature_set_4  <- 
as.matrix(xgb_train_data_transformed_feature_set_4[xgb_selected_features_feature_set_4]) 
xgb_train_label_feature_set_4 <- ifelse(train_data$multimorbidity == "yes", 1, 0) 
 

--- PAGE 160 ---
Investigating the Impact of Dietary Inflammation on Multimorbidity Using the Dietary Inflammatory Index (DII) and Predicting Multimorbidity with 
Machine Learning: NHANES 2015-2018 
  
Dissertation Task 2 160 2360921 
 
xgb_test_matrix_feature_set_4 <- 
as.matrix(xgb_test_data_transformed_feature_set_4[xgb_selected_features_feature_set_4]) 
xgb_test_label_feature_set_4 <- ifelse(test_data$multimorbidity == "yes", 1, 0) 
 
#Creating DMatrix for XGBoost 
xgb_feature_set_4_dtrain <- xgb.DMatrix(data = xgb_train_matrix_feature_set_4, label = 
xgb_train_label_feature_set_4) 
xgb_feature_set_4_dtest <- xgb.DMatrix(data = xgb_test_matrix_feature_set_4 , label = 
xgb_test_label_feature_set_4) 
 
#Setting Parameters for XGBoost 
xgb_feature_set_4_params <- list( 
  booster = "gbtree",        
  objective = "binary:logistic",  
  eta = 0.1,                
  max_depth = 6,            
  gamma = 1,                
  subsample = 0.8,          
  colsample_bytree = 0.8,    
  eval_metric = "error"      
) 
 
#Training the XGBoost Model 
xgb_feature_set_4_bst_model <- xgb.train( 
  params = xgb_feature_set_4_params, 
  data = xgb_feature_set_4_dtrain, 
  nrounds = 100,  
  watchlist = list(train = xgb_feature_set_4_dtrain, eval = xgb_feature_set_4_dtest), 
  early_stopping_rounds = 10,  
  print_every_n = 10 
) 
 
# Predicting the probabilities on the test set 
xgb_feature_set_4_preds <- predict(xgb_feature_set_4_bst_model, xgb_feature_set_4_dtest) 
 
# Convert probabilities to binary labels 
xgb_feature_set_4_preds_binary <- ifelse(xgb_feature_set_4_preds > 0.5, 1, 0) 
 
## Evaluate model performance 
conf_matrix_xgb_feature_set_4<- confusionMatrix(factor(xgb_feature_set_4_preds_binary), 
factor(xgb_test_label_feature_set_4, levels = c(0, 1)),positive = "1") 
conf_matrix_xgb_feature_set_4 
``` 
 
```{r} 
# Setting a seed before cross-validation for consistency 
set.seed(124) 
# Perform Cross-Validation 
cv_xgb_feature_set_4_results <- xgb.cv( 
  params = xgb_feature_set_4_params,

  data = xgb_feature_set_4_dtrain, 
  nrounds = 100,   
  nfold = 5,   
  showsd = TRUE,   
  stratified = TRUE,  
  early_stopping_rounds = 10,   
  maximize = FALSE,

  params = xgb_feature_set_4_params, 
  data = xgb_feature_set_4_dtrain, 
  nrounds = cv_xgb_feature_set_4_best_nrounds, 
  watchlist = list(train = xgb_feature_set_4_dtrain, eval = xgb_feature_set_4_dtest), 
  early_stopping_rounds = 10,
``` 

#Calculate Quartiles for DII and Categorize Data 
```{r} 
# Calculating quartiles for DII 
DII_quartiles <- quantile(NHANES_final_completed$DII, probs = c(0.25, 0.5, 0.75)) 
DII_quartiles 
 
# Extracting DII_quartiles 
q1 <- DII_quartiles[1]  # 25th percentile (first quartile) 
q2 <- DII_quartiles[2]  # 50th percentile (median, second quartile) 
q3 <- DII_quartiles[3]  # 75th percentile (third quartile) 
 
# Categorizing DII into quartiles based on the calculated quantiles 
NHANES_final_completed <- NHANES_final_completed %>% 
  mutate(DII_quartile = case_when( 
    DII <= q1 ~ "Q1", 
    DII > q1 & DII <= q2 ~ "Q2", 
    DII > q2 & DII <= q3 ~ "Q3", 
    DII > q3 ~ "Q4" 
  )) 
 
# Ensuring the new quartile variable is a factor with ordered levels 
NHANES_final_completed$DII_quartile <- factor(NHANES_final_completed$DII_quartile, 
levels = c("Q1", "Q2", "Q3", "Q4")) 
 
# Print the counts of each quartile 
table(NHANES_final_completed$DII_quartile) 
```

```{r} 
# Train the random forest model  
rf_model_train_adult <- randomForest( 
  multimorbidity ~ DII + age_category + BMI+ gender + ethnicity, 
  data = train_data_adult, 
  ntree = 500, 
  importance = TRUE) 
 
rf_pred_adult <- predict(rf_model_train_adult, test_data_adult[,-7], type= "class")

test_data_adult$multimorbidity,positive = "yes") 
conf_matrix_adult 
 
# Random forests training + tuning 
 
# Define the control parameters for tuning 
ctrl_parameters <- trainControl(method = 'cv', number = 4) 
 
# Train the Random Forest model with tuning

ethnicity, data = train_data_adult, method = "rf", trControl = ctrl_parameters) 
 
# Inspect the result of the tuning 
cv_rf_tuned_model_adult 
 
set.seed(124) 
# predictions on the test set after tuning 
cv_rf_tuned_pred_adult <- predict(cv_rf_tuned_model_adult, newdata = test_data_adult[, -
7]) 
 
# Create a contingency table for the actual vs. predicted values 

--- PAGE 166 ---
Investigating the Impact of Dietary Inflammation on Multimorbidity Using the Dietary Inflammatory Index (DII) and Predicting Multimorbidity with

f1_score_adult
``` 

```{r} 
test_data_senior$multimorbidity, positive = "yes")
``` 

####Variable importance plot for subgroup analysis 
```{r} 
# Extracting the random forest model from the 'train' object 
rf_model_middle_age <- cv_rf_tuned_model_middle_age$finalModel 
rf_model_adult <- cv_rf_tuned_model_adult$finalModel 
rf_model_elderly <- cv_rf_tuned_model_elderly$finalModel 
rf_model_senior <- cv_rf_tuned_model_senior$finalModel 
 
rf_model_male <- cv_rf_tuned_model_male$finalModel 
rf_model_female <- cv_rf_tuned_model_female$finalModel 
 
rf_model_mexican_american <- cv_rf_tuned_model_mexican_american$finalModel 
rf_model_non_hispanic_white <- cv_rf_tuned_model_non_hispanic_white$finalModel 
rf_model_Non_Hispanic_Black <- cv_rf_tuned_model_Non_Hispanic_Black$finalModel 
 
# Calculating variable importance 
#age category 
importance_rf_cv_middle_age <- as.data.frame(importance(rf_model_middle_age)) 
importance_rf_cv_middle_age$Variable <- rownames(importance_rf_cv_middle_age) 
importance_rf_cv_middle_age$Subgroup <- "Middle Aged" 
 
importance_rf_cv_adult <- as.data.frame(importance(rf_model_adult)) 
importance_rf_cv_adult$Variable <- rownames(importance_rf_cv_adult) 
importance_rf_cv_adult$Subgroup <- "Young Adult" 
 
importance_rf_cv_elderly <- as.data.frame(importance(rf_model_elderly)) 
importance_rf_cv_elderly$Variable <- rownames(importance_rf_cv_elderly) 
importance_rf_cv_elderly$Subgroup <- "Elderly" 
 
importance_rf_cv_senior <- as.data.frame(importance(rf_model_senior)) 
importance_rf_cv_senior$Variable <- rownames(importance_rf_cv_senior) 
importance_rf_cv_senior$Subgroup <- "Senior" 
 
#gender 
importance_rf_cv_male <- as.data.frame(importance(rf_model_male)) 
importance_rf_cv_male$Variable <- rownames(importance_rf_cv_male) 
importance_rf_cv_male$Subgroup <- "Male" 
 
importance_rf_cv_female <- as.data.frame(importance(rf_model_female)) 

--- PAGE 179 ---
Investigating the Impact of Dietary Inflammation on Multimorbidity Using the Dietary Inflammatory Index (DII) and Predicting Multimorbidity with 
Machine Learning: NHANES 2015-2018 
  
Dissertation Task 2 179 2360921 
 
importance_rf_cv_female$Variable <- rownames(importance_rf_cv_female) 
importance_rf_cv_female$Subgroup <- "Female" 
 
#ethnicity 
importance_rf_cv_mexican_american <- 
as.data.frame(importance(rf_model_mexican_american)) 
importance_rf_cv_mexican_american$Variable <- 
rownames(importance_rf_cv_mexican_american) 
importance_rf_cv_mexican_american$Subgroup <- "Mexican American" 
 
importance_rf_cv_non_hispanic_white <- 
as.data.frame(importance(rf_model_non_hispanic_white)) 
importance_rf_cv_non_hispanic_white$Variable <- 
rownames(importance_rf_cv_non_hispanic_white) 
importance_rf_cv_non_hispanic_white$Subgroup <- "Non-Hispanic White" 
 
importance_rf_cv_Non_Hispanic_Black <- 
as.data.frame(importance(rf_model_Non_Hispanic_Black)) 
importance_rf_cv_Non_Hispanic_Black$Variable <- 
rownames(importance_rf_cv_Non_Hispanic_Black) 
importance_rf_cv_Non_Hispanic_Black$Subgroup <- "Non-Hispanic Black" 
 
# Combining the importance data for plotting 
combined_importance <- rbind(importance_rf_cv_middle_age, importance_rf_cv_adult,  
                             importance_rf_cv_male, importance_rf_cv_female,  
                             importance_rf_cv_elderly, importance_rf_cv_senior, 
importance_rf_cv_mexican_american, importance_rf_cv_non_hispanic_white, 
importance_rf_cv_Non_Hispanic_Black) 
 
# Setting the order of the Subgroup levels 
combined_importance$Subgroup <- factor(combined_importance$Subgroup,  
                                       levels = c("Young Adult", "Middle Aged", "Senior", "Elderly",  
                                                  "Male", "Female",  
                                                  "Mexican American", "Non-Hispanic Black", "Non-Hispanic 
White")) 
 
# Preparing the data for ggplot2 
importance_melted <- melt(combined_importance, id.vars = c("Variable", "Subgroup"),  
                          variable.name = "Metric", value.name = "Importance") 
 
# Plotting the variable importance for each subgroup 
ggplot(importance_melted, aes(x = Variable, y = Importance, fill = Subgroup)) + 
  geom_bar(stat = "identity", position = "dodge") + 
  labs(title = "Variable Importance by Subgroup", x = "Variable", y = "Importance (Mean 
Decrease in Gini)") + 
  theme_minimal() + 
  theme(axis.text.x = element_text(angle = 45, hjust = 1)) 
```

```{r} 
# Random Forest - middle_age 
rf_prob_middle_age <- predict(cv_rf_tuned_model_middle_age, test_data_middle_age[,-
which(names(test_data_middle_age) == "multimorbidity")], type= "prob")[,2]

test_data_middle_age$multimorbidity)
``` 
